12386{_}1122{_}That wuz Aunt Tryphena's greatest condemnation to say folks lacked.
12386{_}1123{_}She never told what they lacked, but left it to the imagination of the hearer; from her expression you would imagine they lacked all the cardinal virtues and them that wuzn't cardinal.
12386{_}1124{_}She said his ma wuz sick and kep' the Prince right under her feet, and he'd gone back now to be with her leaving St. Louis only a week or so before we come.
12386{_}1125{_}Bein' asked why she left Miss Louise she wuz more reticent, only remarking that after Prince Arthur went to college she wanted a change, so she had strolled over to South America, and from there to Asia and so on to Chicago where she wuz hired as nurse to Miss Dotie, and when her ma died and the child wuz taken by its great-aunt, Miss Huff, she had been willing to help the latter through the Exposition, for she wuz a nice woman and didn't lack.
12386{_}1126{_}But we could see that her real reason wuz to be with the child--faithful creeter she wuz, though queer, queer as they make.
12386{_}1127{_}And to see the little creature's white snow and rose face resting lovingly and confidingly aginst the black cheeks, you knew that Aunt Tryphena had good in her.
12386{_}1128{_}Little children are good detectives, like the sun that photographs hidden virtues and failings in the human face, so a child's intuition brought from the heaven they have so lately left, takes the best impressions of a person's real character.
12386{_}1129{_}Children and animals live so near Nature's heart they can detect real diamonds from the false, no paste glitter can deceive 'em.
12386{_}1130{_}Aunt Pheeny had qualities, or Dotie wouldn't have loved her so well, and I felt it a great compliment that she seemed to like me.
12386{_}1131{_}Well, as observed heretofore we had took a hefty job that day, and we proceeded first to the Educational Buildin'.
12386{_}1132{_}It wuz a noble lookin' structure with a row of snowy pillows all 'round it; a good many think it is the handsomest buildin' on the Fair ground, and as I said to Josiah, it ort to be considerin' the greatness and importance of the work it displays, for our free schools, our educational advantages, are the pride and glory of our country.
12386{_}1133{_}"Yes, Samantha," sez he, "I hearn a man say yesterday education wuz the very bull work of our country, meanin' you know, Samantha, it wuz strong as a bull."
12386{_}1134{_}"Oh, you hain't got it jest right, Josiah, bulwark don't mean jest that, but you've got the sperit of it," I hastened to say, for he don't love to be corrected.
12386{_}1135{_}And here in this buildin' we see everything relating to schools from kindergarten to university, training schools, where children wuz to work, schools for the blind, deaf and dumb in operation; the work of labratories going on before you; departments in drawing, music, agricultural colleges; experiment stations, forestry, engineering schools and institutions, libraries, museums, education of the Indian and negro, evening industrial schools, business and commercial schools, people's institutes, and every way and manner of mind training.
12386{_}1136{_}Photograph, charts, maps, and not only all our own educational exhibits, but England, France, Germany, Russia, China, and in short all the foreign countries.
12386{_}1137{_}We stayed a good while there and I would have loved to stay longer, but Josiah got worrisome and wanted to go on to Electricity Buildin' which wuz next in our programmy.
12386{_}1138{_}And here I took more solid comfort than in any place I'd been, beholdin' the marvelous works wrought by the greatest discovery of the ages.
12386{_}1139{_}That wonderful Force that has power to overcome space, save or slay.
12386{_}1140{_}It is intelligent, can talk over the ocean and under it, talk with wires, and if a wire hain't handy it will take a beam of light and talk on that, and it can git along without either one, for here is the biggest wireless telegraph station ever built; visitors can talk on it from city and city, jest throwin' their words out into the air and this onseen agency carries 'em along to the one sent to and nobody else--wonderful hain't it?
12386{_}1141{_}Wonderful to meditate on the great onseen forces all about us, mysterious viewless shapes, nigh to us, helpin' us, journeyin' on errents of mercy to and fro on paths we can't see, leadin' up and down from star to star from heaven to earth mebby.
12386{_}1142{_}And curious, hain't it, that the noble and ardent discoverers who have tried to git friendly with them Great Forces and introduce 'em to the world have been called ignorant and pagan, when if these scoffers knowed it there is no paganism or ignorance to be compared to that of bigotry and intolerance.
12386{_}1143{_}And we see there dynamos of all kinds, motors, storage batteries, all sorts of power machines.
12386{_}1144{_}Electric railway equipments of every kind, telephone stations for talking with wires and without 'em, all kinds of electric lighting, arc lamps, electro-chemical displays.
12386{_}1145{_}And in one place they show the way Niagara wuz made to yield up her resistless power to work for mankind.
12386{_}1146{_}Labratories for all sorts of electrical exhibits and research work.
12386{_}1147{_}Electricity purifying water, making it safe to drink, wuz one of its best exhibits.
12386{_}1148{_}There wuz everything there it wuz possible to show in electricity and magnetism, not only in our own country, but the work and discoveries of all the foreign countries in this most interestin' of fields.
12386{_}1149{_}There is another wireless telegraph and telephone station in the Model City that we visited another time.
12386{_}1150{_}You walk into this room and you don't hear anything more than the ordinary noise the big crowd makes passin' to and fro.
12386{_}1151{_}And the air about you don't seem any different from jest plain Jonesville air.
12386{_}1152{_}Your human eyes and ears can't discover any difference.
12386{_}1153{_}But you jest take up a receiver and put it to your ear and lo, and behold the atmosphere all about you is full of voices, near and fur off, strains of music.
12386{_}1154{_}It's a sight.
12386{_}1155{_}And I sez to Josiah, "Who knows but some happy soul some happy day may discover the secret of _seeing_?
12386{_}1156{_}Who knows what divine visitors are this minute coming and going over these onseen routes connecting our souls with distant ones, connecting one land to another, one planet to another like as not."
12386{_}1157{_}And growin' some eloquent, I kep' on, "We don't hear the sound of their footsteps lighter and more noiseless than the down of a blossom, shod as they are with the softness of silence.
12386{_}1158{_}We don't hear the rustle of their garments, woven of frabic [sic] lighter than air.
12386{_}1159{_}We can't see their tender faces no more than we can see the sweet breath of the rose.
12386{_}1160{_}If they lay their tender hands on our foreheads they rest there so light and tender we fancy it is only a breath of air touchin' our fevered brows bringing a sudden rest and comfort.
12386{_}1161{_}"If they speak to us when we're tired out and heartbroken we hear their voices only in our souls that are suddenly and strangely consoled.
12386{_}1162{_}If their eyes ever look into our eyes filled with the divine pity and sweetness of their all comprehendin' love and sympathy, we only know it by the sudden sunshiny light and warmth that fills our being.
12386{_}1163{_}But sometime, somewhere, some happy soul may see and comprehend what we now faintly apprehend."
12386{_}1164{_}Josiah whispered, "Samantha Allen, do you realize what you're doin'?
12386{_}1165{_}You're attractin' attention and makin' talk, come along!
12386{_}1166{_}this is no time for eppisodin', if there ever _is_ a right time."
12386{_}1167{_}And bein' brung down to earth agin I found to my great surprise I wuz sayin' this out loud entirely unbeknown to myself.
12386{_}1168{_}And I follered my pardner out of the buildin'.
12386{_}1169{_}But to resoom backwards.
12386{_}1170{_}We thought we would go from the Palace of Electricity to that of Transportation, and I feelin' real tired thought I would take a chair a spell (eloquence is tuckerin' specially when you're walkin' afoot), and I proposed that we should all take chairs for a spell.
12386{_}1171{_}But Josiah said he didn't want any chair, and Blandina of course follered suit and said she felt jest like Uncle Josiah, she wouldn't set down if she could.
12386{_}1172{_}But I sez, "Well, I think I will take one," and Josiah ruther onwillin'ly said he would git one for me, and sez he, "I'll see how much the man will throw off if I push the chair myself."
12386{_}1173{_}Sez I, "The man wouldn't trust a perfect stranger with a chair."
12386{_}1174{_}Then Josiah wondered if he couldn't borry the loan of a wheelbarru that would hold me up.
12386{_}1175{_}He could trundle me along as well as not.
12386{_}1176{_}Sez I, "I shall not enter the Palace of Transportation, Josiah Allen, in a wheelbarrow."
12386{_}1177{_}"Well, I could probable git in Machinery Hall a pair of big castors and fix 'em onto your shoes, and Blandina and I could push you 'round like a buro.
12386{_}1178{_}What do you think of that?"
12386{_}1179{_}sez he anxiously.
12386{_}1180{_}"I shall not enter into any such operation!"
12386{_}1181{_}sez I.
12386{_}1182{_}"How it would look!"
12386{_}1183{_}"I d'no as it would look so dretful, you standin' up straight and easy, and Blandina and I pushin' you along, and 'tennyrate I guess it would look as well as bein' throwed onto the town!
12386{_}1184{_}chairs cost like the old Harry."
12386{_}1185{_}Sez I, "Don't worry, I shall pay with my own butter money."
12386{_}1186{_}And so I did, and rid to Transportation Buildin' with Josiah and Blandina walkin' by my side.
12386{_}1187{_}We entered one of its sixty doors, and the first thing we sot our eyes on up in plain sight, but fur ahead wuz the wheels of a great locomotive weighin' more than two hundred thousand pounds, revolvin' 'round in dizzy speed.
12386{_}1188{_}They said it went by compressed air, another wonder, jest common air that you could dip up in your hand and not think you had anything in it, and yet if managed right had power enough to turn all the machinery we see goin'.
12386{_}1189{_}Around this monster engine wuz electric head-lights throwin' dazzlin' beams in every direction.
12386{_}1190{_}The hull thing well named, the Spirit of the Twentieth Century.
12386{_}1191{_}And all 'round it wuz grouped models showing the development of the inventor's dream from the first rough effort at an engine up to the most perfect specimen of to-day.
12386{_}1192{_}All sorts of electrical railways, freight and work cars, tracks, switches, signals, carriages, ortomobiles, motor vehicles, naval architecture, models, boats, steamships, men-of-war, battleships of the line.
12386{_}1193{_}Exhibits of all sorts, illustrating inland transportation in India, France, Germany, Switzerland, Spain and every other foreign country.
12386{_}1194{_}You could see to once that there wuz ways enough to travel, and if you stayed to home it wuz your own fault.
12386{_}1195{_}Well, we went from there to Machinery Buildin', that bein' writ down next on my pad.
12386{_}1196{_}But as we walked along, I considerable riz up in my mind, owin' to what I'd seen, who should we come acrost but the widder Whisher of Loontown, a woman we knew well.
12386{_}1197{_}She wuz settin' on a bench cryin' as if her heart would break, and I sez:  "Why, sister Whisher, what is the matter?"
12386{_}1198{_}(She wuz sister in the meetin' house.)
12386{_}1199{_}She had a paper in her hand and held it out to us, "Jest see that!
12386{_}1200{_}I found it in the pocket of my innocent boy!"
12386{_}1201{_}pintin' to a coat layin' by her.
12386{_}1202{_}"Why," sez I, "that paper is took more than any other almost; I like it myself first-rate, its editorials are the brightest and smartest you'll find anywhere."
12386{_}1203{_}"Oh, but it is so sensational!
12386{_}1204{_}so vulgar, so demoralizin' to the tender and innocent heart of youth.
12386{_}1205{_}And to think that my spotless child that I have guarded so sedgously from every breath of evil should have it concealed in his pocket.
12386{_}1206{_}I have always burnt every copy I've found."
12386{_}1207{_}And agin she sobbed, and agin I sez:  "Sister Whisher, don't take it so to heart; he'll have to weather worst storms than this on the sea of life.
12386{_}1208{_}And you can't expect to be with him always and stand to the hellum."
12386{_}1209{_}"Oh, but Reginald Heber is so innocent, so pure-hearted; almost an angel," sez she, "I have been so afraid that he wuz too perfect for this sinful world!"
12386{_}1210{_}And her tears flowed afresh.
12386{_}1211{_}Well, I see I couldn't plug up this flowin' fountain of tears with sympathy or reason, so we mogged along.
12386{_}1212{_}Widder Whisher wuz always kinder soft and she'd made a perfect idol of Reginald, who wuzn't any better than common children so fur as I could see.
12386{_}1213{_}And after goin' a few steps, Josiah and I in advance, Blandina a little in our rears, who should we see comin' directly towards us but Reginald Heber himself.
12386{_}1214{_}He evidently didn't notice who we wuz, but wuz merely takin' note of a new victim, for after takin' fair aim at my stomach he bent his head down and went, "Choo, choo!--choo, choo!"
12386{_}1215{_}like a engine and run towards me at full speed, and bunted his round shingled head right into my stomach with almost the force of an arrer shot out of a catamount, yellin' all the while like a demon.
12386{_}1216{_}"Git out of the way, you old four-eyed devil you!"
12386{_}1217{_}Makin' light of my spectacles, I spoze, though truly I wuz too weak to reason.
12386{_}1218{_}After doublin' me up in agony he sought safety in flight.
12386{_}1219{_}But my indignant pardner ketched him by his little short-tailed coat and dragged him back to his ma, hollerin' at her:  "I'll give you a specimen of your innocent boy!
12386{_}1220{_}He's jest the kind of an innocent angel I'd love to take a hemlock shingle to, and would, if it wuzn't for makin' talk."
12386{_}1221{_}And he told the hull thing before I could interfere.
12386{_}1222{_}She wept afresh, but sez she, lookin' at the whimperin' and strugglin' Reginald H., "How soon the demoralizin' effects of that paper shows----"  But Josiah continued on in that same loud axent, his liniment red as blood with anger, "If I had your darling to deal with a spell, there would be a change in him, or a funeral appinted, and the body would be ready at the time sot, I can tell you that!"
12386{_}1223{_}Josiah wuz fearful excited and by the side of himself.
12386{_}1224{_}Such voylent language is almost a perfect stranger to him, but he feared for my bones.
12386{_}1225{_}But I found after walkin' 'round a spell that they wuz intact, but the pain in my stomach hung about me all day, and that night, no matter how high my standin' wuz in the W.C.T.U., I had to take a peppermint sling.
12386{_}1226{_}But to resoom backward.
12386{_}1227{_}Machinery Buildin' wuz an immense beautiful palace.
12386{_}1228{_}And when I tell you its contents are valued at eight millions you won't expect me to disscribe the hull on 'em, no, it hain't reasonable.
12386{_}1229{_}When we entered we see the first thing a engine of over fifty thousand horse-power.
12386{_}1230{_}Now, jest think on't, a one horse-power hain't to be despised.
12386{_}1231{_}Why, I've thought our old mair power when she wuz hitched onto a bob sled wuz powerful.
12386{_}1232{_}But jest think of fifty thousand horse-power.
12386{_}1233{_}Why, if they wuz hitched in front of each other with lines about the usual length, the line would reach more than a hundred miles.
12386{_}1234{_}Why, the very idee is staggerin' to the intellect.
12386{_}1235{_}But, there it was right there before our eyes grindin' out power to run this monster Exposition, and not complainin' or needin' the whip as the fifty thousand horses would, only jest knucklin' down stiddy to the work, groanin' considerable loud, and who blames it.
12386{_}1236{_}And you could see everything in the line of engines from the little half horse-power gas engine, about half the mair's strength, about cow power, mebby, and from this up to a steam turbin of eight thousand horse-power, a rotary steam engine.
12386{_}1237{_}And in the Belgian exhibit wuz a gas engine of three thousand horse-power, a common sized horse can be driv through its cylinders, it takes about thirty tons of coal a day to run it.
12386{_}1238{_}And there wuz a big French steam engine turnin' three hundred and thirty times a minute.
12386{_}1239{_}And there wuz a great hydraulic press from Germany that exerts the terrific pressure of ninety thousand pounds to the square inch--what would it be to the yard?
12386{_}1240{_}My brain hain't powerful enough to tackle the idee.
12386{_}1241{_}Well, there wuz every kind of machinery in the world from all the foreign countries as well as ours, and the methods of making and running them.
12386{_}1242{_}And we stayed there till my head seemed to turn 'round and 'round, and I told my pardner I must git out into the open air or I should begin to turn 'round and revolve in spite of me.
12386{_}1243{_}I spoze I did look bad, and Josiah said we would go and have lunch.
12386{_}1244{_}He said there wuz a caff right 'round the corner, as he pronounced cafe it sounded like a young cow.
12386{_}1245{_}But the idee wuz good, and after we eat quite a good meal and rested a little we started to tackle Agricultural Buildin' which wuz writ next on my pad.
12386{_}1246{_}It wuz quite a journey there, in fact, as I've said before, you have to walk a long distance to git anywhere, but jest before we got there we see sunthin' that made us forgit for the moment our achin' limbs.
12386{_}1247{_}On the side of a slopin' hill at the bottom of the long flight of stairs, that lead up to the north entrance of Agricultural Hall is the most wonderful clock that wuz ever seen on this globe, and I don't believe they've got anything to beat it in Mars or Saturn.
12386{_}1248{_}I can't give you much idee of it by writin', nobody can, but I can probably describe it so you can see it goes ahead of your own clock on the kitchen wall or mantelry piece.
12386{_}1249{_}To begin with how long do you spoze the minute hand is?
12386{_}1250{_}The minute hand on our clock is about three inches long, and the minute hand to this is fifty feet long, and its face is about three hundred feet 'round and all made of the most beautiful posies.
12386{_}1251{_}Why, the figures that mark the hours are fifteen feet long, most three times as long as my pardner, if he lay flat as a pan-cake to be measured by a pole, jest think of that and these figgers are all made of bright colored foliage plants.
12386{_}1252{_}The ornaments 'round the face of the clock is a border of twenty-five different plants, each one fifteen feet wide.
12386{_}1253{_}Some different from the ornamental wreath 'round our clock face, that hain't more'n half an inch wide, if it is that.
12386{_}1254{_}Our clock has a picture underneath of old Time with his scythe a mowin' down the hours and minutes as his nater his.
12386{_}1255{_}And I told Josiah how beautiful and symbolical it wuz to think old Time had laid down his scythe for a spell, and wuz measurin' off the hours here in this Fairy Land with beautiful posies.
12386{_}1256{_}And Josiah said, "The hours ort to be marked here with canes and crutches," he said his legs ached like the toothache.
12386{_}1257{_}The distances are awful and I couldn't deny it, and you do git tuckered out, but then, as I told Josiah, jest think what you're tuckered for.
12386{_}1258{_}And he said, "When you're as dead as a door-nail he didn't know what good some steeples and flags wuz goin' to do you, or floral clocks."
12386{_}1259{_}I mistrusted he'd walked too fur lately, and had strained the cords of his legs, and his patience too much, though the last-named wuz easy hurt and always wuz.
12386{_}1260{_}But Josiah took out his watch and looked at it and said he'd promised to meet a man on important bizness, and he'd meet us at a certain spot in Agricultural Hall in jest one hour.
12386{_}1261{_}I asked him what bizness it wuz, and he hesitated a little and said as he hurried away that it wuz "Bizness connected with the meetin' house," and I asked him "What meetin' house?"
12386{_}1262{_}and he didn't answer me, he wuz walkin' off so fast--_mebby_ he didn't hear me.
12386{_}1263{_}Well, Blandina and I stayed lookin' at this wonderful clock for some time, and she said that the man that invented this clock wuz a powerful genius and how she did wish she could meet him.
12386{_}1264{_}She said such a man needed a kind and lovin' companion to take every care offen him and pet him and make of him.
12386{_}1265{_}The machinery of this clock, what makes it go, is up above a little ways on the hill in a small pavilion.
12386{_}1266{_}There are glass doors, and you can look in and see the works of the clock.
12386{_}1267{_}A great bell there strikes off the hours and quarter hours, and there is a big hour-glass there too.
12386{_}1268{_}One thousand electric lights light it up at night so folks can see day or night jest how time is passin' away.
12386{_}1269{_}Agricultural Building is the largest on the ground.
12386{_}1270{_}The two palaces of Agriculture and Horticulture stand up on a beautiful hill surrounded by orchards, gardens, vineyards, shrubs, vines of all sorts.
12386{_}1271{_}This outside exhibit covers fifty acres.
12386{_}1272{_}There are beautiful lakes full of the rarest aquatic plants, from the great Egyptian lotus, whose leaves are large and strong enough to hold up a good-sized child, and all kinds of smaller plants, but jest as beautiful; indeed, there is everything rare and lovely in that display that ever grew in water or on land, and they make it one of the most beautiful places of the hull Exposition.
12386{_}1273{_}The enormous display outside and inside covers seventy acres, and every inch on 'em beautiful and instructive.
12386{_}1274{_}The twenty acres covered by Agricultural Hall contains everything relating to the soil and its cultivation, everything that Mother Earth gives to man, all the tools, implements of every kind used in agriculture, ploughs, reapers, mowers, threshers, etc., run by horse-power, steam or electricity.
12386{_}1275{_}Among the ploughs we see a small old-fashioned one made of wood, used by Daniel Webster when he wuz a poor farmer boy.
12386{_}1276{_}Workin' hard at his humble work but his boyish mind, most probable, sot on sunthin' fur above, lookin' at the hard soil ahead on him that he must break up, with them wonderful, sad, eloquent eyes of hisen, and seein' visions, no doubt, and dreamin' dreams.
12386{_}1277{_}Callin' out to his oxen or horses, "gee," or "whoa" as the case might be, and they not sensin' the fact that this voice wuz goin' to give utterance to silver-tongued, heart thrillin' eloquence in the highest places of Europe and his native land.
12386{_}1278{_}As I looked at it pensively I pictured the tired boy holdin' the onhandy handles of the plow and trudgin' along behind his team through the long sultry days, and thought to myself, what hopes and dreams and ambitions wuz turned over by that old plow as well as green-sward.
12386{_}1279{_}Right by that little plow wuz a big powerful one that went by electricity.
12386{_}1280{_}A sight that would probable looked as strange to Daniel, could it have appeared to him then, as any of his wildest day-dreams materilized.
12386{_}1281{_}And there wuz all the methods of irrigation, draining, engines, wind-mills, pumps, farm wagons, all kinds of fruit, sugar canes, vegetable sugar, candy stores, confectionery displays, vegetables of all kinds that wuz ever hearn on, some on 'em of such monster size that you never dremp on 'em, unless it wuz in a night-mair.
12386{_}1282{_}CHAPTER VIII.
12386{_}1283{_}Well, the time had arrived when we promised to meet Josiah at the appinted rondevoo.
12386{_}1284{_}Indeed Blandina, went a little ahead of time, for as second chaperone she said it might be he would get there a little early, and bein' naturally high-sperited he might get impatient, and she said men ort to be guarded from anything that would wear on their tempers, jest as much as possible.
12386{_}1285{_}So I looked 'round a little more, and when I got to the place appinted, there sot Blandina readin' extracts from "The Noble Achievements of Men" in a paper cover, which she carried 'round in her pocket.
12386{_}1286{_}But no Josiah wuz there.
12386{_}1287{_}Minutes passed; my happiness and peace of mind passin' off faster than the minute hand, and no Josiah.
12386{_}1288{_}A quarter of a hour passed, and still no sign of that dear man.
12386{_}1289{_}And when half an hour had gone by I busted into tears, and Blandina I could see wuz torn with anxiety and offered to go out into the streets of St. Louis and hunt for him.
12386{_}1290{_}She mistrusted he had wandered off the Fair ground, and that clever creeter wuz willin' to leave all the allurements that wuz allurin' her here to hunt for him.
12386{_}1291{_}I sez, "I don't believe he is there.
12386{_}1292{_}But, oh, where shall we find him?
12386{_}1293{_}and what state will he be in when found!"
12386{_}1294{_}Knowin' the past as we did, we feared for the worst.
12386{_}1295{_}But jest then Billy Huff happened to pass by and stopped and asked what wuz the matter.
12386{_}1296{_}"Oh!"
12386{_}1297{_}sez I, with the tears runnin' down my cheeks in copious as torrents, "my pardner is lost!"
12386{_}1298{_}"Where did you lose him?"
12386{_}1299{_}sez he.
12386{_}1300{_}I told him how it wuz and he sez, "I'll bet I can find him for you; I remember his talkin' last night about a certain place."
12386{_}1301{_}[Illustration]  Sez I in tearful axents, "Oh, do!
12386{_}1302{_}do try, and ease the heart of a distracted companion."
12386{_}1303{_}But when he mentioned the place he thought he wuz I repelled the insinuation with scorn.
12386{_}1304{_}It wuz one of the most hilarious and vain places of revelry at the Fair, where there wuz lots of bally girls and etcetery, and I sez:  "No, indeed!
12386{_}1305{_}He may have gone into some meetin' house and wandered up into the steeple onbeknown to him, or some educational exhibit, or Bible rooms, but never, never in that place."
12386{_}1306{_}But yieldin' to his arguments I consented to go with him sayin' we would stay at the door while he reconoitered.
12386{_}1307{_}But jest as we got to the door who should we see comin' out radiant and smilin' but Josiah Allen and Uncle Sime Bentley.
12386{_}1308{_}Billy sez, "What did I tell you?"
12386{_}1309{_}I couldn't frame a reply, I had no frame that fitted the remark, but as Billy disappeared to once it didn't matter.
12386{_}1310{_}When Josiah ketched my eye and the look it wore, the blush of shame mantiled his cheek--or wuz it remorse?--I couldn't tell, they look some alike.
12386{_}1311{_}And he sez, "We went in, Samantha, to look for a missin' man, and my corn ached like furiation jest as we wuz passin' the door, and I couldn't seem to walk another step, and it looked some like rain and I knew you wouldn't want me to spile my new coat----"  And Uncle Sime chimed in, "We wuz took faint both on us jest as we got to the door and had to set down, and I mistrusted I should find cousin Zekiel there," and then happenin' to remember, both at the same time, they begun to say how they went for the good of the meetin' house.
12386{_}1312{_}Sez I in frigid axents, "Say no more!"
12386{_}1313{_}And I turned onto my heel and walked coldly away.
12386{_}1314{_}But Blandina whispered to me, "Oh, be merciful, Aunt Samantha, men have such powerful intellects, that Shows that would almost ruin a woman, don't affect them hardly any.
12386{_}1315{_}Speak tenderly to him," sez she, "and I myself will gently accost Mr.
12386{_}1316{_}Bentley."
12386{_}1317{_}So she stepped back to his side and Josiah advanced and walked by me still pourin' out excuses.
12386{_}1318{_}Why he gin enough reasons to excuse a regiment let alone one small deacon.
12386{_}1319{_}But Blandina seemed to lose her efforts, for Uncle Sime talked real grouty to her, he has never had a idee of marryin' anybody since his wife died and he mistrusts wimmen are runnin' after him.
12386{_}1320{_}You know male widowers do git that idee into their heads, them that are as humbly as Time in the Primer, and a onmarried woman can't ask 'em about the weather, or sheep, or anything but what they mistrust some hidden warmth, and pride themselves on how attractive they be.
12386{_}1321{_}It's a sight.
12386{_}1322{_}As nigh as I could find out the minute Josiah Allen left me he took the railway and hurried to the wicked place where he and Uncle Sime wuz to meet, expectin' to git back in ample time to meet us.
12386{_}1323{_}But they wuz so took up with the show they dallied, and so retribution and a indignant pardner overtook 'em.
12386{_}1324{_}Well, we took the Intremoral railway and went back to finish Agricultural Hall, for that bein' writ on my pad I wanted to complete it so fur as we could, of course it would took months to do justice to it.
12386{_}1325{_}We got there in a few minutes, and Josiah, as might be expected, wanted to see the food exhibits, so we went where there wuz all kinds of food made of vegetable products, all kind of grain, flour mills where you could see wheat go in one end and bread come out the other, bakeries, kitchens, tea and coffee pavilions and every sort of animal food products, milk and cream in every form, fresh and preserved cheese and butter dairies, all sorts of dairy tools, churns, separators, cheese presses and vats, everything connected with makin' butter and cheese, transporting and distributing.
12386{_}1326{_}Starch factories, broom factories, market gardening in all branches.
12386{_}1327{_}Grasses, all sorts of fodder for cattle, raised in every country of the world, and the best methods of raising.
12386{_}1328{_}Everything relating to poultry, artificial hatching and raising.
12386{_}1329{_}Every kind of crop raised in every country of the world and the best methods of raising and handling them.
12386{_}1330{_}As in cotton, you can see it from the tiny seed clear to the cotton mill, so in corn, you see everything that is manufactured from it and how it is done--meal, breakfast foods, starch, bread, pastry, baking powders, yeast, from a kernel of corn up to mills and manufactories.
12386{_}1331{_}And so it wuz in everything raised in our own country and all over the world.
12386{_}1332{_}And there wuz a display of insects, bees and everything relating to honey and wax.
12386{_}1333{_}Silk worms and their work and products, cochineal and all kinds of useful insects and their work, and hurtful insects and methods of destroying them, and so on and so on and so on.
12386{_}1334{_}I couldn't tell all I see if I should try a week, and what we see wuzn't a drop to a fountain.
12386{_}1335{_}The immense buildin' is divided off into streets and blocks jest like a city, and you might roam through them streets a month and find sunthin' new and interestin' every day and hour.
12386{_}1336{_}Well, from there we went to Horticultural Hall, or we had started for there when Josiah made a observation about the size of a potato he had seen in Agricultural Hall, that I had to in the cause of Truth and Duty object to, the size he mentioned was a twelve-quart pail, and I said:  "Josiah, take off a few quarts from that pail.
12386{_}1337{_}For the good of your soul take off two quarts anyway."
12386{_}1338{_}"Not a quart!"
12386{_}1339{_}sez he, "nor a spunful."
12386{_}1340{_}Well, we had words about it, Blandina as usual siding with her uncle, and it ended with their goin' back with a string, which Josiah produced from his pocket to measure it, I offering to stay by a certain statute till they got back.
12386{_}1341{_}And as I stood there lookin' at the stiddy passin' crowd and philosophizin' on it as my nater is, I wuz accosted by a strange lookin' man, as I took it to be (I say It for reasons named hereafter).
12386{_}1342{_}"Josiah Allen's wife, I am happy to meet you; I knew you at once though it is so long since we met."
12386{_}1343{_}In the meantime it had gripped holt of my hand with fervor.
12386{_}1344{_}I drawed back and sez, "Sir!"
12386{_}1345{_}(I thought it favored that gender most) "Sir, I think you are mistook."
12386{_}1346{_}"Oh, no, you are Josiah Allen's wife; I am Dr. Mary Walker."
12386{_}1347{_}"Oh!"
12386{_}1348{_}sez I in a relieved axent, as I returned the warm grasp of her hand, "I am glad to meet you, Mary."
12386{_}1349{_}She's done some good things in her life, takin' care of poor wounded soldiers, etc., and I honored her for 'em.
12386{_}1350{_}Though I don't approve of her costoom, as I told her in the conversation that ensued, after we'd talked considerable about the Fair and kindred matters.
12386{_}1351{_}For I see as we stood there behavin' ourselves, curious eyes wuz bent on her and onbecomin' epithets hurled at her by them who knowed no better.
12386{_}1352{_}She seemed oblivious to 'em, but I asked her if she wouldn't rather wear less noticeable attire.
12386{_}1353{_}And she said she cared not for ribald remarks as long as her motives wuz pure.
12386{_}1354{_}And I said we could carry pure motives under a headdress of peacock's feathers standin' up straight over our foreheads, but wouldn't it be better to carry 'em under a bunnet?
12386{_}1355{_}"No better!"
12386{_}1356{_}sez she.
12386{_}1357{_}"Not a whit."
12386{_}1358{_}"Well, easier?"
12386{_}1359{_}sez I.
12386{_}1360{_}"Wouldn't it be easier for ourselves and bystanders?"
12386{_}1361{_}Sez she, "I care not for Public Opinion!"
12386{_}1362{_}"But," sez I, "as long as we've got to live clost neighbor to Public Opinion wouldn't it be easier for us to fall in with his idees a little on comparatively unimportant things than to keep him riled up all the time?
12386{_}1363{_}It seems to me that if folks want to impress their personality on the world it is better to do it by noble deeds and words than by startlin' costooms."
12386{_}1364{_}Sez she, "My dress is fur more comfortable than the ordinary dress of females."
12386{_}1365{_}Sez I reasonably, "Short dresses are a boon and a blessin', but in my opinion they can be short enough for comfort and still not infringe on man's chosen raiment.
12386{_}1366{_}And as for pantaloons, men are welcome to 'em so fur as I'm concerned, and also tall hats, they hain't nothin' I hanker for either on 'em."
12386{_}1367{_}Sez she, "We have a right to wear any clothes we see fit."
12386{_}1368{_}Sez I, "We have a right to plow green sword, shingle a steep barn ruff, or break a yoke of steers.
12386{_}1369{_}But the question is, will it pay in comfort or economy to do this?
12386{_}1370{_}As for me, I'd ruther be in the house in a comfortable dress and clean apron, cookin' a good dinner for Josiah, or settin' down knittin' his socks whilst he duz the harder work he is by nater and education fitted for.
12386{_}1371{_}But everybody to their own mind.
12386{_}1372{_}And so fur as I am concerned I'd ruther attract attention by doin' sunthin' worth while, sunthin' really noble and good, than by tyin' a red rag round my fore-top.
12386{_}1373{_}But as I say, folks are different, and I am fur from sayin' that my way is the only right way."
12386{_}1374{_}Mary kinder waived off some of my idees and went on and spoke of her work on the battlefield and how necessary her dress wuz in such a place.
12386{_}1375{_}And I sez, "Mary, I've always honored you for your noble work there.
12386{_}1376{_}But I believe I could lift up the head of a dyin' man easier in a loose gingham dress and straw bunnet tied on, than I could in your tight pantaloons and high hat, but howsumever the main thing is that the man is lifted, and he doubtless wouldn't quarrel about the costoom of his preserver.
12386{_}1377{_}The main thing in this world, Mary, is the work we do, the liftin', or tryin' to lift; the day's work we do in the harvest field of Endeavor.
12386{_}1378{_}And I spoze a few trousers more or less hain't goin' to count when we carry in our sheaves.
12386{_}1379{_}Though I must say to the last, Mary Walker, I could carry 'em easier in my dress than I could in yourn."
12386{_}1380{_}[Illustration]  In the heat of our good-natered conversation Mary had slipped her hand through my arm and neither of us noticed it, so wropped up wuz we in the topics under discussion, when I hearn Blandina's voice behind me sayin', "Oh, what a noble lookin' man Aunt Samantha is talkin' to and how affectionate actin'; how sweet it will be to meet him."
12386{_}1381{_}And then I hearn a sharp raspin' voice clost to me sayin':  "Sir, I will thank you to onhand my wife!"
12386{_}1382{_}I wouldn't hardly have knowed my pardner's voice, such burnin' anger showed in it and wuz depictered on his liniment as I turned round and faced him.
12386{_}1383{_}And he went on:  "Samantha, have I lived with you most a century to be deceived in you now?"
12386{_}1384{_}His turrible emotions had onhinged his reasonin' faculties, we hain't lived together so long as that, but I didn't dane to argy, I only sez with calm dignity:  "Miss Walker, this is my pardner, Josiah Allen."
12386{_}1385{_}"_Miss_!"
12386{_}1386{_}sez he in a overbearin' axent, "_Miss_ Walker!"
12386{_}1387{_}He looked as if he thought it wuz a conspiracy hatched up between us to deceive him.
12386{_}1388{_}"Yes," sez I coolly, "Miss Walker, Dr. Mary Walker."
12386{_}1389{_}"Oh!"
12386{_}1390{_}sez Josiah, in his surprise and relief not offerin' to bow or shake hands or nothin'.
12386{_}1391{_}"Dear Samantha, I've hearn on her."
12386{_}1392{_}And he turned and linked his hand in my other arm so for a minute we looked like three twins perambulatin' along.
12386{_}1393{_}In the meantime I introduced Blandina, who looked bewildered and disappointed.
12386{_}1394{_}But Dr. Mary Walker remembered a engagement, and to my relief took leave on us.
12386{_}1395{_}And I said a few words to Josiah on the danger and cruelty to me of his hasty opinion and suspicion and in the cause of Duty I mentioned the late eppisode of himself and Uncle Sime, and he seemed mortified and apologetic for as many as three minutes.
12386{_}1396{_}But it didn't last, it never duz with his sect.
12386{_}1397{_}And we went on to Horticultural Hall, Josiah on the way reluctantly showin' me the string he had measured the potato with.
12386{_}1398{_}He had to take off several quarts offen that pail, jest as I told him he would, and it made him fraxious.
12386{_}1399{_}But he lost his shagrin on the way, it wuz buried under the acres of posies and beautiful shrubs and trees through which we wuz passin'.
12386{_}1400{_}Every rare posy you ever hearn on wuz there and them you never dremp on, and trees, some beautiful and familiar, and them with strange and beautiful foliage.
12386{_}1401{_}Little lakes, where gold and silver fish played and dotted over with the rarest and loveliest water plants and blossoms, shrubs runnin' over with bloom, why, there wuz acres of jest rosies.
12386{_}1402{_}And in the middle of a six-acre rose garden stood a handsome statute of one of my own sect, Flora by name, jest lookin' down as if she owned the hull on't, and wuz proud and happy to be there, as well she might--she'll never git into such a delightful spot agin, I don't believe.
12386{_}1403{_}And there wuz pleasant walks windin' round every which way and once in awhile a big tree shadin' a cozy nook where you could sit down and enjoy the beauty and perfume.
12386{_}1404{_}It wuz good to be there, and it seemed as if the hull world had the same mind about comin' and wuz all there walkin' about or else settin' down enjoyin' themselves.
12386{_}1405{_}Horticultural Buildin' is big enough and full enough to keep folks busy a month.
12386{_}1406{_}Right in the centre, in a place as long as from our house clear over to she that wuz Submit Tewksbury's and I d'no but furder, wuz a display of fruit, all kinds of fruit of every shape and size that grow in every climate from frigid to torrid, and every country from Greenland to Asia, it wuz a sight.
12386{_}1407{_}Then there wuz a display of every kind of horticultural machinery and implements, glass housen, aquariums, ferneries, all sorts of ornaments for gardens.
12386{_}1408{_}All kinds of small fruits and how to grow 'em, everything relating to the culture of vines, vineyards, wine cellars.
12386{_}1409{_}All sorts of ornamental plants and flowers, models of fruit in wax and plaster, baskets and bunches of flowers, conservatories, all flowering plants from every country and the way to grow them.
12386{_}1410{_}All sorts of seeds, grass, fruit trees of all kinds, and the best way to prune and plant them.
12386{_}1411{_}Josiah told me he thought we could git round and see what wuz in this buildin' in four weeks, but I felt dubersome about it and told him we would have to go a pretty good jog if we did.
12386{_}1412{_}Blandina thought she could git round in three weeks if she had some good man's arm to lean on the most of the time.
12386{_}1413{_}But 'tennyrate, after stayin' there and lookin' round a long time, I told Josiah I wuz tired enough to go home, so we went.
12386{_}1414{_}I wuz most melted too, for St. Louis weather is tuckering to them that can't stand heat.
12386{_}1415{_}It made Josiah real worrisome time and agin.
12386{_}1416{_}And one thing he said about it put a idee into my head that I never had thought on, I thought it wuz real smart.
12386{_}1417{_}Somebody wuz lamentin' the fact in our hearin' that so many thieves and villains of all sorts had congregated at St. Louis this summer, and Josiah sez:  "It's a first rate thing for sinners to come here to git acclimated, as it were, before they die."
12386{_}1418{_}I hadn't thought on't, but felt there wuz sunthin' in it, for truly the burnin' climate of the place I don't want to speak on by name, must be easier to bear after visitin' St. Louis than to plunge into it from cooler and more northern States.
12386{_}1419{_}And still I don't know why we should want to make it easier for 'em, I spoze it wuz our pityin' naters that made us think ont.
12386{_}1420{_}The weather wuz simply burnin' hot, no other word describes it, oveny, furnacy hot!
12386{_}1421{_}and Josiah said, and well said, it set folks to thinkin' and inclined 'em to take warnin' and mend their ways.
12386{_}1422{_}Sez he, "Two days of St. Louis weather wuz worth more to sinners than the sermons of a month of winter Sundays."
12386{_}1423{_}Truly in heat it wuz a great object lesson.
12386{_}1424{_}I wore my brown lawn dress day after day, havin' no chance to wear my rich alpacky, as I wanted to, to kinder show off before Miss Huff, and Blandina presented the wilted appearance of a long slim cabbage leaf plunged in bilin' water.
12386{_}1425{_}I believe Josiah's groanin's and takin's on and mutterin's helped him to bear it better than if he had held in.
12386{_}1426{_}Not that I told him so, no, I told him it wuz onmanly to carry on so.
12386{_}1427{_}But truly the heat wuz fearful, our clothin' stuck to us and prespiration and sweat run down our faces.
12386{_}1428{_}The next day it wuz so hot I felt kinder mauger and stayed to home.
12386{_}1429{_}Blandina and Miss Huff went half a day, and in the afternoon Blandina went to a big department store in the city to git some thinner underwear, and I got awful skairt about her.
12386{_}1430{_}Miss Huff gin her the most minute directions about where it wuz and what car to take, it wuzn't a great ways off, and she ort to got back at four o'clock anyway.
12386{_}1431{_}But time run along, four struck, then five and then six, and I wuz gittin' dretful worried about her when she come in tired enough.
12386{_}1432{_}Sez I, "I wuz awful worried about you, Blandina.
12386{_}1433{_}Did you git lost?"
12386{_}1434{_}"No."
12386{_}1435{_}She said she got onto the right car and the conductor wuz a dretful handsome and fascinatin' man, and she went to git off at the right street, and kinder backed off, she always duz git off that way, and the conductor thinkin' she wanted to git on, he smiled so sweet and held out his hand to help her on so she would git on again.
12386{_}1436{_}And that happened over and over.
12386{_}1437{_}She not wantin' to hurt his feelin's and slight him by not takin' holt of his hand and climbin' on agin.
12386{_}1438{_}Till finally she did show some good sense, she asked the man standin' on the platform if he would help her off, for she had been tryin' to git off for the last five stations.
12386{_}1439{_}So she had to take a car back, but the conductor wuz humbly and gruff and she got along all right, but it belated her.
12386{_}1440{_}Sez I, "What made you do it, Blandina?"
12386{_}1441{_}"Oh," sez she, "he looked so winnin' and invitin' I didn't want to hurt his feelin's."
12386{_}1442{_}Sez I, "You'll sup sorrer yet, Blandina, by your wantin' to obleege everybody.
12386{_}1443{_}You ort to look out for yourself some, you're alltogether too good to be comfortable."
12386{_}1444{_}CHAPTER IX.
12386{_}1445{_}Well, Josiah went that day with Billy Huff, he santered off without any system or plan, and wouldn't take my pad though I offered it to him.
12386{_}1446{_}But I guess they jest poked round miscelaneous, as you may say, seein' jest what they happened to run into.
12386{_}1447{_}And in some of their travels they met Barzelia Trimble, a woman lecturer, she's young and good lookin' and smart as a whip, and I guess she made much of Josiah, 'tennyrate she gin him tickets to her lecture.
12386{_}1448{_}She said she'd met a man whose brother-in-law's cousin had bought a dog once of a neighbor of mine, and so feelin' so well acquainted with me she sent me the tickets, and did hope we would come.
12386{_}1449{_}She said she felt that she knew us both so well that it would be a treat to her.
12386{_}1450{_}The way she come to see Josiah that day, Billy had met her at school where she lectured.
12386{_}1451{_}Josiah wuz very anxious that we should both go.
12386{_}1452{_}He remembered the dog.
12386{_}1453{_}But I sez, "I thought you didn't believe in wimmen's lecturin' and havin' rights, Josiah."
12386{_}1454{_}"Well, I don't believe in 'em, but the tickets wuz gin to us, fifty cents right out of her pocket, and she'll expect us.
12386{_}1455{_}She said it would make her feel more homelike to have us present."
12386{_}1456{_}"Well," sez I, "I don't know as I feel so very intimate with her, I never see the dog, but her idees on wimmen's rights is sensible, I've read about 'em."
12386{_}1457{_}And that kinder headed Josiah off onto a new tact; we had had a dretful good supper, and I believe Miss Trimble had made a sight on him, I believe she had flattered and pompeyed him and for the time bein' he felt soft in sperit towards the sex.
12386{_}1458{_}And 'tennyrate men's moods are like the onfathomable sea, sometimes turbulent, throwin' up stunny arguments and sandy ones, and agin flowin' calm and smooth as ile, and this wuz one of the gently swashin' ones.
12386{_}1459{_}"Id'no," sez he, "and I told her so, what wimmen want rights for, or to vote; I never wanted wimmen to vote, I told her they wuz too good, they wuz too near angels to have rights.
12386{_}1460{_}You know I've always said so, Samantha, and I wuz readin' a piece a day or two ago, writ by one of the first ministers in the country, and he said that wimmen hadn't ort to want any rights; they ort to be riz up on a pedestal and I say so too."
12386{_}1461{_}And I sez, "No, Josiah, I can't go into that with all the rest I have to do, and it seems onreasonable in that minister to want wimmen to climb up onto pedestals when they have to do their own housework."
12386{_}1462{_}"Well, I say it hain't onreasonable.
12386{_}1463{_}You ort to be up on one, Samantha."
12386{_}1464{_}(How much Miss Trimble must have made on him.
12386{_}1465{_}He wuz so oncommon clever, and he never wuz megum, poor creeter!)
12386{_}1466{_}I didn't really want to git into an argument at that time o' day, but I see he wuz on the wrong tact, and I felt I must convince him, so I sez in reasonable axents:  "I jest as lives be on a pedestal as not, I'd kinder love to if I could set, I always did enjoy bein' riz up, if I had nothin' to do only to stay up there some time, but wimmen have to git round so much it wouldn't work.
12386{_}1467{_}How could I take a tower histed up like the car of Juggernaut or a Pope in a procession.
12386{_}1468{_}I couldn't get carriers for one thing, and I wouldn't give a cent to be carried round anyway with my dizzy spells, I should more'n as likely as not fall off.
12386{_}1469{_}But that hain't the main reason I'm agin it, it is too tuckerin' a job for wimmen."
12386{_}1470{_}"Tuckerin' to be enthroned on a pedestal with the male sect lookin' up to you and worshippin' you.
12386{_}1471{_}You call that tuckerin'?"
12386{_}1472{_}sez he.
12386{_}1473{_}"Yes," sez I, "I do.
12386{_}1474{_}How under the sun can I or any other woman be up on a pedestal and do our own housework, cookin', washin' dishes, sweepin', moppin', cleanin' lamps, blackin' stoves, washin', ironin', makin' beds, quiltin' bed quilts, gittin' three meals a day, day after day, biled dinners and bag puddin's and mince pies and things, to say nothin' of custard and pumpkin pies that will slop over on the level, do the best you can; how could you keep 'em inside the crust histin' yourself up and down?
12386{_}1475{_}And cleanin' house time----"  "Mebby," sez I honestly, "it would come handy in whitewashin' or fixin' the stovepipe, but where would it be in cleanin' mop-boards, or puttin' down carpets, or washin' winders, or doin' a three weeks washin', or bilin' soap?
12386{_}1476{_}or pickin' geese?
12386{_}1477{_}They act like fury shot up on the barn floor.
12386{_}1478{_}How could you git our old gander up on a pedestal?
12386{_}1479{_}His temper is that fiery, to say nothin' of settin' or standin' on it and holdin' on to the old thing and pickin' it.
12386{_}1480{_}And raisin' chickens and washin' old trousers and overalls, and cleanin' sullers and paintin' floors and paperin', and droudgin' round all the time, as a woman has to to keep her house comfortable.
12386{_}1481{_}"And pickin' black-caps and strawberries, and churnin' big churnin's of butter, and pickin' wool, to say nothin' of onexpected company comin', and no girl.
12386{_}1482{_}Let a lot of company come to stay all day the relations on your side and the work not done, and me posin' like a statute, lookin' down on you and your sect, you'd feel like a fool and jaw, you know you would.
12386{_}1483{_}I presoom you'd throw your boot-jack at me and threaten to part with me, and how mean that would be in you when I did it at your request.
12386{_}1484{_}'Tain't anything any woman would go into if she wuz let alone."
12386{_}1485{_}"And then think of the thrashers and silo fillers comin' in hungry as bears, what would they say?
12386{_}1486{_}No dinner cookin' and I on a pedestal, why it would be the town's talk.
12386{_}1487{_}Or you comin' home from Jonesville on a cold night fraxious as a dog and sayin' you should die off if you didn't have supper in ten minutes.
12386{_}1488{_}How could I git it on time perched up there?
12386{_}1489{_}"I say it can't be done, and it is onreasonable for men to want it, and at the same time want wimmen to do her own housework.
12386{_}1490{_}For these men, every one on 'em, would act like fury if their house wuzn't clean and their clothes in order, and meals on time.
12386{_}1491{_}And you must know it would jest about kill a woman to be doin' all this and histin' herself up and down a hundred times a day, and mebby half dead with rumatiz too.
12386{_}1492{_}Why, it would be worse for me than all the rest of my work, and you hadn't ort to ask it of me."
12386{_}1493{_}Josiah looked real huffy and sez, "I hain't the only man that's wantin' it done; men have always been sot on it.
12386{_}1494{_}There's been more'n a wagon load of poetry writ on it and you know it.
12386{_}1495{_}Men have always said a sight about it, I hain't alone in it," he snapped out.
12386{_}1496{_}"No," sez I honestly, "I've hearn it before.
12386{_}1497{_}But you see it wouldn't work, don't you?
12386{_}1498{_}And I believe I could convince every man if I could git to 'em and talk it over with 'em.
12386{_}1499{_}And I don't see where the beauty on't would come in; of course a woman couldn't change her clothes and put on Greek drapery right in the midst of cleanin' the buttery shelves or moppin' off the back steps.
12386{_}1500{_}And to see a woman standin' up on a pedestal with an old calico dress pinned up round her waist and a slat sunbunnet on and her pardner's rubber boots, and her sleeves rolled up, and her face red as blood with hard work, and her hands all swelled up with hot soap suds and lye, what beauty would there be in it?
12386{_}1501{_}It always did seem onreasonable besides bein' so tuckerin' no woman could stand it for a day."
12386{_}1502{_}He looked mad as a hen and sez he, "They could manage it if their minds wuz strong enough."
12386{_}1503{_}Sez I, "It seems to me it would depend more on the strength of their legs, specially if the pedestal wuz a high one.
12386{_}1504{_}I never could git up onto it at all if I should go into it without gittin' up on a chair and then on a table.
12386{_}1505{_}No woman no matter how strong she wuz could git more than two meals a day under the circumstances."
12386{_}1506{_}Josiah looked worried and sez, "Well, mebby there has been too much said about it, mebby it would be jest as well to leave pedestals to statters."
12386{_}1507{_}And I sez, "It is as well agin.
12386{_}1508{_}Wimmen couldn't stand it with all they have to do."
12386{_}1509{_}And so we ended by bein' real congenial in our two minds and thinkin' considerable alike, which is indeed a comfort to pardners.
12386{_}1510{_}And we read our chapter in the Bible and had family prayers jest as we do to home.
12386{_}1511{_}For I would not leave off all the good old habits of my life because my body wuz moved round a little.
12386{_}1512{_}And we had a good night's rest and sot out in good season the next mornin' for the Exposition.
12386{_}1513{_}The next mornin' grandpa Huff said to the breakfast table that he did wish he had someone to read to him that day, everybody wuz goin' to the Fair and he wuz goin' to be left alone.
12386{_}1514{_}So Blandina, clever creeter that she is, said she would stay and read to him from his favorite volume, Foxe's Book of Martyr's, and also from Lamentations and Job.
12386{_}1515{_}Billy said his grandpa wuz never happy only when he wuz perfectly miserable.
12386{_}1516{_}We have all seen such folks.
12386{_}1517{_}So Josiah and I sot off alone, and he bein' in good sperits and bein' gin to new and strange projects, proposed that we should take an ortomobile.
12386{_}1518{_}I didn't favor the idee and said:  "Id'no about it, Josiah, I feel kinder skairful about ortos, I fear that it might prove our last ride."
12386{_}1519{_}"But," sez he, "with a good shuffler there hain't any danger."
12386{_}1520{_}But I still wuz dubersome and sez, "Mebby it would end by our shufflin' off our mortal coils, as Mr. Shakespeare tells on."
12386{_}1521{_}"You don't wear 'em, Samantha, nor never did, nor I don't wear a pompodoor" (he meant this for a joke for his head is most as bare as a sass plate).
12386{_}1522{_}And he went on, "It would be a very stylish and genteel ride.
12386{_}1523{_}I'd love to tell brother Gowdey about it.
12386{_}1524{_}The bretheren will expect it of me as a live progressive Jonesvillian minglin' here with the noblest in the land to cut sunthin' of a dash."
12386{_}1525{_}But seein' that I still looked dubersome he sez, "I don't feel very rugged this mornin' and I dread the crowded car; Id'no but I should faint away in 'em if I sot out."
12386{_}1526{_}That of course settled the matter.
12386{_}1527{_}As his anxious chaperone I consented to the project and he went and got the showiest one he could find.
12386{_}1528{_}He didn't look for character or stability, only for gildin' and red paint.
12386{_}1529{_}And we embarked, Josiah with a proud liniment, as if he wuz introducin' me into gay life and fashionable amusements.
12386{_}1530{_}The man wuz to take us to the Fair ground for so much, and Josiah feelin' so neat had paid him in advance, and there wuz another party waitin' for him.
12386{_}1531{_}And the speed that shuffler put on wuz sunthin' awful.
12386{_}1532{_}The first few minutes before we got to goin' that terrific speed Josiah liked it, and seemed to look patronizin'ly down on the people walkin' afoot that we passed by and pity 'em.
12386{_}1533{_}But anon the man got to goin' faster and faster and Josiah's liniment underwent a change and he hollered out to me, for the noise wuz so loud and skairful he had to yell:  "Samantha, I don't believe it is right for members of the meetin' house to be goin' at such a gait."
12386{_}1534{_}And I hollered back to him, "It hain't none of my doin's, it hain't nothin' I wanted," I a hangin' onto my bunnet strings and tryin' to keep my bunnet on.
12386{_}1535{_}As for the tabs of my mantilly I had gin up tryin' to curb 'em down, and they waved out like a pirate's flag in a cyclone only a different color.
12386{_}1536{_}Finally Josiah hollered to the shuffler, "I want you to curb in your machine!
12386{_}1537{_}I'm a deacon, and have got my station in the Jonesville meetin' house to think on.
12386{_}1538{_}Hold it in, I say!"
12386{_}1539{_}The shuffler glanced round at us as calm as a goggle-eyed clam and never dained to answer, and seemin'ly urged on the orto to redoubled speed.
12386{_}1540{_}Oh, the awfulness of the seen!
12386{_}1541{_}the terrific noise soundin' on my ear pans till it seemed as if them pans must break down, the dirt a flyin', my pardner standin' up with his whiskers and coat tails wavin' in the breeze.
12386{_}1542{_}His hat blowed off and by almost superhuman exertions I ketched it and carried it in my hand, thinkin' it wuz safer than on his head.
12386{_}1543{_}He a yellin', "Stop, I tell you!
12386{_}1544{_}Whoa!
12386{_}1545{_}back up!
12386{_}1546{_}Dum your dum picter, whoa I say!"
12386{_}1547{_}For the last few milds Josiah rid standin' all I could do and say.
12386{_}1548{_}Yellin' at the shuffler, hollerin' whoa to him, and appealin' to Heaven and me simultaneous as it were, for mercy and succor.
12386{_}1549{_}[Illustration]  And that shuffler payin' no more attention to him than as if he wuz a fly, not a hoss fly, but jest a common fly.
12386{_}1550{_}Only he would look back at us once in awhile through them big goggles of hisen that most curdled my blood to see 'em.
12386{_}1551{_}At last Josiah, seemin' to give up all hope, sunk back and grasped holt of my tab and sez, "Good-bye, Samantha, if you git through alive remember I died tryin' to save you."
12386{_}1552{_}His emotions and the dirt choked him, and he faintly added:  "Tell the bretheren and see that it is put in the Jonesville Augur, that I died a hero's death tryin' to save my pardner."
12386{_}1553{_}And his grasp on my tabs become almost hysterical.
12386{_}1554{_}But at that minute the entrance gate wuz reached and the orto stopped so abruptly, that Josiah who had got up agin, wuz precipitated into my lap.
12386{_}1555{_}But he got out immegiately, and the minute he and I stepped onto terry firmy he turned and shook his fist at the man and sez he, "If it wuzn't for the crowd and Samantha's feelin's, I would whip you within an inch of your life!
12386{_}1556{_}Oh, if I only had you in a ten acre lot you'd feel the wrath of a lion when it wuz rousted up!"
12386{_}1557{_}But I laid my hand on him and led him away, I knowed such seens wuz bad for his nerve.
12386{_}1558{_}He trembled like a popple leaf, and the minute we got through the gate I had to set down with him and deal out four nut-cakes before he wuz himself agin.
12386{_}1559{_}I wuz determined this day to go to the Palace of Fine Arts, so we did and I put in a time of almost perfect happiness there.
12386{_}1560{_}We went into Government Building entrance that day, and I proposed to Josiah that we should stop at Liberal Arts Building on the way, and he at first demurred and sez:  "Samantha, you're too liberal by half now for folks with our means and Id'no as I want you to spend your time in such a display."
12386{_}1561{_}He said he would rather take me to the display of Economics, and sez he, wantin' to persuade me to go with him, "Wimmen has countless virtues, but to my mind her crownin' excelence is to be equinomical."
12386{_}1562{_}But I explained to him that exhibit didn't mean bein' liberal with money but it wuz jest a step behind Fine Arts, and sez I, "I should think you would want to see the place where this Exposition wuz dedicated in the presence of one of the biggest crowds that wuz ever gathered together."
12386{_}1563{_}So we stopped there a little while, and could have spent days there with interest and profit.
12386{_}1564{_}The foreign countries have splendid exhibits here as well as our own.
12386{_}1565{_}Everything in typography and books, everything possible in photography; models of light-houses; dams; geographical maps; Egyptian, Hebrew and Imperial surveys.
12386{_}1566{_}Scientific demonstrations in liquid hydrogen and that queer substance, radium.
12386{_}1567{_}I wuz dretfully interested in that wonderful new discovery and sez I to myself as I looked at it, "As little as there is of you there is enough to overturn big systems of science and philosophy, and begin a new history of the inside of the world."
12386{_}1568{_}I wuz glad my sect had discovered this and thought it wuz one of the best things she had done in a number of years.
12386{_}1569{_}And there wuz all kinds of hygienic displays, chemical and engineering works.
12386{_}1570{_}China had a dretful interestin' exhibit, ancient manuscripts, books published thousands of years before our kind of type wuz invented.
12386{_}1571{_}Weapons that wuz old when Mr. Confucious wuz livin'.
12386{_}1572{_}Armor, costumes, musical instruments, queer lookin' things them wuz as I ever see and nothin' I would want to play on.
12386{_}1573{_}Photo engineering, electrotyping, lithography, typewriting; telescopes of all kinds from tiny ones up to ones that weigh four thousand pounds.
12386{_}1574{_}The latest medical and surgical instruments.
12386{_}1575{_}The piano from the first one made up to the present automatic instruments of all kinds; stringed instruments, church organs; displays in civil and military engineering; machinery for making good roads; rock crushers, water purifying, and so on and so on and so on.
12386{_}1576{_}The time spent in this buildin' is full of education as well as interest.
12386{_}1577{_}There wuz some beautiful statutes too decoratin' this buildin', most on 'em I wuz proud to see wuz figgers of my own sect.
12386{_}1578{_}But having sot out for the Palace of Fine Arts we anon wended our way thither.
12386{_}1579{_}It is a beautiful building, or ruther there are four massive buildings connected together to form this Palace of Art.
12386{_}1580{_}There are three big buildings in front and an annex, the central building built of stone and brick is the only permanent buildin' in this enormous Exposition so naturally they would make it as perfect as possible.
12386{_}1581{_}And it is crowded full of beauty.
12386{_}1582{_}In fact turn where you would you would see such glowing landscapes, such beautiful faces, such perfect sculpture that you git all mixed up, and when you thought it over you couldn't remember whether some picture or statute that stood out in your memory wuz in the U.S. exhibit or the French, or German, or Italian, or etc., etc.
12386{_}1583{_}In lookin' back and thinkin' on't and tryin' to git 'em in the right place in your mind it is as difficult as it would be in walking through a big clover meadow and tryin' to sort out the clover blossoms and describe 'em one by one and tell in jest what corner of the lot you found 'em.
12386{_}1584{_}It can't be done; in such an immense field of art your brain sort o' fills up and turns round and round and you git mixed.
12386{_}1585{_}But as I say some of the pictures and statutes stayed in my memory so I couldn't dislodge 'em and don't want to, no indeed!
12386{_}1586{_}Now there are three noble figgers at the entrance that you can't forgit.
12386{_}1587{_}Inspiration standin' up above the main entrance is jest where she should be.
12386{_}1588{_}Inspiration, breath of the Most High breathed into some of His children below anon or oftener, and then on each side is Truth and Nature.
12386{_}1589{_}Nature, the kind All Mother, Truth, the divine one.
12386{_}1590{_}How sweet to find 'em all there together guardin' and consecratin' these walls.
12386{_}1591{_}You went in feelin' safer with such gardeens at the portal.
12386{_}1592{_}I must say though that Truth didn't have any clothes on, she wuz jest settin' there on top of the world jest as naked as she could be, she could have wore one of my bib aprons as well as not, durin' the Fair anyway, whilst there wuz so many folks round and she would have looked enough sight better to me and been jest as truthful.
12386{_}1593{_}But howsumever I knew she wuz likely, her face wuz innocent and beautiful.
12386{_}1594{_}As I said it is some of the pictures and statutes that stand out clearest in my memory, but there wuz everything else there admirable and choice in art, paintings in oil, wax; on canvas, wood, enamel, metal, fresco paintings on walls and ceilings.
12386{_}1595{_}Water colors, chalk, pastel, ivory, pyrography.
12386{_}1596{_}Engravings, etchings, figgers in marble, metal, plaster.
12386{_}1597{_}Carvings in ivory, stone, wood, etc.
12386{_}1598{_}Architectural designs of all kinds; mosaics; art work in glass, earthen ware, leather, metal; artistic book binding and etc., etc., etc., and I might spread these out into volumes.
12386{_}1599{_}And didn't my soul jest spread her wings here in delight, to speak in flowery language.
12386{_}1600{_}What pictures of beauty dawned on my rapt eyesight, faces sweet as wuz ever dremp on, sad faces, tragic faces, old faces and young faces; children sweet and bonny as wuz ever seen.
12386{_}1601{_}Youth and love, age and manhood and gratified ambition, princes and paupers, life and death.
12386{_}1602{_}Landscapes full of the dewy freshness and joy of the morning, night seens dark and full of mystery and melancholy.
12386{_}1603{_}Mountain and valley, hill and dale, ocean and rivulet.
12386{_}1604{_}Every phase of human joy and sorrow wuz depictered there, and every phase of peaceful and warlike life.
12386{_}1605{_}It wuz a sight.
12386{_}1606{_}If I could stayed there a year right in them walls I might have got round mebby and seen what I wanted to and as long as I wanted to.
12386{_}1607{_}But of course this wuzn't to be, for one thing the Fair would be closed before and then Josiah wouldn't gin his consent anyway.
12386{_}1608{_}He got kinder worrisome as it wuz and didn't want to stay so long as we did, and after a hour or so I compromised with him, gin him nut cakes occasionally and anon when we would enter a new gallery he would set down by the door till I had got through lookin'.
12386{_}1609{_}As I said some of the pictures and statutes clung to my memory as if they'd been throwed at my mind so powerful that they jest stuck there and couldn't be dislodged even by all the later multitude of sights throwed over 'em.
12386{_}1610{_}There wuz one by Whistler full of the subtle mystery that he wrops round his figgers.
12386{_}1611{_}Why you know he has painted one that to them that are sympathetic, the Little Lady in Black, will walk right out of the picture and come towards 'em, time and agin she's done it, I'm tellin' the truth that can be proved.
12386{_}1612{_}In the "Mystery of the Night," the female figger dimly discerned through the veil of mist seems the incarnation of the mystery of sky and sea, the infinite solemnity, and peace and loneliness of the night.
12386{_}1613{_}There wuz pictures that made you happy, and some that sort o' sent a chill to your sperit, like Millais' "Chill October," as you looked at it you almost felt the chill, mournful breeze that you knew wuz sweepin' along.
12386{_}1614{_}Some queer pictures like the "Ghost Dance" kinder lingered in the vestibule of your mind.
12386{_}1615{_}You know your mind has got more different rooms in it than any house that wuz ever built, and some pictures and folks don't git into the very inmost rooms; they never git furder than the doorstep.
12386{_}1616{_}There are three pictures by the King and Queen of Portugal, all on 'em picturin' humble life.
12386{_}1617{_}The King's show a peasant drivin' cattle to water.
12386{_}1618{_}I wondered if he didn't wish, when he painted it, that he wuz that care-free herder, who could sing and whistle and wear easy shues, and throw on any old clothes, and santer out into the dewy mornin' and do as he wanted to.
12386{_}1619{_}One of the Queen's wuz a farm wagon, such as they carry farm produce in, but sometimes I spoze load up with merry girls and boys for a happy outing in the green woods.
12386{_}1620{_}I shouldn't wonder if when she wuz dead tired of the cares, formalities and burdens of a queen, she wished she wuz one of them happy young girls riding off in a cotton frock on the old farm wagon into some joyous picnic.
12386{_}1621{_}The other one of hern wuz a cute little donkey and over all on 'em wuz bright sunlight and soft shadow.
12386{_}1622{_}They done well.
12386{_}1623{_}I wished I could encouraged 'em by tellin' 'em so--a word of praise sometimes duz so much good, to anybody from peasant to king.
12386{_}1624{_}Among the statutes that I see to the Fair that stood up straight in my mind wuz Light and Darkness.
12386{_}1625{_}Darkness wuz in the form of two men, one on 'em crouched low with his arm over his face drawin' his mantle to hide from the light.
12386{_}1626{_}The other male is liftin' his head but his eyes are still shot, evidently he feels the dawn of sunthin' better and he's waking up, while standin' erect is the graceful figger of a female, beautiful and noble, full of boundin' life and light, holdin' up high over her head a star.
12386{_}1627{_}She wants to wake up the hull world to the light.
12386{_}1628{_}Dakota wuz pictured as a lady with precious few clothes on; she looked old in her face, and I told Josiah it wuz a shame to see a woman that age with such a low-necked dress on.
12386{_}1629{_}It wuz cut down to the bottom of her waist.
12386{_}1630{_}And lots of the men staters wuz wearin' low necks.
12386{_}1631{_}I didn't like it, but Josiah remarked that he'd always said:  "A vest and coat cut low neck would make a man look dressy, and he believed he should have one made for best."
12386{_}1632{_}I looked coldly at him and said it looked bad enough to see young folks dress in that way without old folks cuttin' up and actin'.
12386{_}1633{_}Lots of the statutes would looked as well agin if they'd had me to advise 'em about their clothes, but still take the pictures and statutes of the Fair as a hull they're magnificent and a honor to the nations.
12386{_}1634{_}There are a thousand statutes, all beautiful and inspirin', to be seen there on the Exposition grounds.
12386{_}1635{_}I wuz glad to see the statute of Dr. Jenner, who discovered vaccination, tryin' it first on his own son.
12386{_}1636{_}When it is the law for doctors to try their medicine first on their own folks, miscelaneous patients will feel safer.
12386{_}1637{_}Dr. Jenner acted honorable toward humanity at large.
12386{_}1638{_}I told Josiah I hoped the boy got along well and didn't git hit on the arm while it wuz sore.
12386{_}1639{_}And he said, "I wouldn't worry over folks I never neighbored with, and I'd better tend to my own companion, who wuz starvin' slowly by my side."
12386{_}1640{_}He couldn't been so very hungry havin' eat so many nut-cakes since breakfast, but I dealt out some more to him.
12386{_}1641{_}Well, we stayed in the Art Gallery a long time, so long that Josiah complained bitterly and sez, "If you stay as long in every buildin' when will we git round to see the Pike?"
12386{_}1642{_}Truly Josiah longed for that place day by day, but as first chaperone of the party I tried to delay him from goin', knowin' that it must come sometime but gladly puttin' off the day.
12386{_}1643{_}But I sez soothin'ly, "I shan't want to stay so long at any other place."
12386{_}1644{_}And it bein' past our lunch time we went and had a good meal, and of course Josiah's crossness subsided with every mouthful he took and his liniment looked like a cosset lamb's in amiability when I proposed we should go to the Fishery Buildin', it wuzn't so very fur from there considerin', though as I have said before every place is a good ways off from anywhere else.
12386{_}1645{_}You'd have knowed the buildin' by the great fish that wuz sculped over the entrance.
12386{_}1646{_}It wuz a bigger fish than wuz ever lied about in male fish stories, and that's sayin' enough; connected with this is also an exhibit of forestry and game.
12386{_}1647{_}We went into the part devoted to forestry first, there are several acres outdoors as well as inside devoted to this display, and what didn't we see there in trees, plants, woods of every kind, forest growth tree planting, all sorts of useful wood, pine, spruce, hemlock, cedar, all the hard woods, and everything made of wood; wood pulp, barrels, baskets, turpentine, alcohol.
12386{_}1648{_}In the United States exhibit wuz immense pictures illustrating our forests, methods of lumbering, lumber camps, forest fires, etc., etc.
12386{_}1649{_}There wuz displays of different species of trees and plants, forest botany, structure and anatomy of woods, saw-mills, seeds and plants of all kinds, and all the different woods and products of wood from Egypt to Japan, barks, roots, cork, rubber, gums, oils, quinine, camphor, varnish, wax, dye-woods, lumber, staves, why there wuz over two hundred different kinds of wood from Argentina alone.
12386{_}1650{_}Josiah, who wuz real interested here, sez, "I'd love to have brother Gowdey step in here a minute; he's proud as a peacock of his strip of woodland, he thought he covered the hull field of forestry with his wood pulp and maple sugar.
12386{_}1651{_}I guess his pride would be took down a little."
12386{_}1652{_}"Well," sez I, "let's look on it as showin' the greatness and wonder of Providence and be humble and admire."
12386{_}1653{_}"I shall look at it as I'm a minter!"
12386{_}1654{_}he sez.
12386{_}1655{_}But I guess he wuz more reverential for a spell.
12386{_}1656{_}And there wuz all the plants and leaves used in medicine, and mushrooms, truffles, seeds and plants and implements for gathering and preserving; drying houses, nurseries, basket work, grass work.
12386{_}1657{_}It seemed as if everything that could be known about trees and plants could be learnt here, and though we knowed we hadn't time or convenience to take all the knowledge in, no, our heads wuzn't big enough, but they felt crowded full as we left this buildin'.
12386{_}1658{_}And that I felt wuz the crownin' glory of this fair, the new idees and knowledge of better ways and things that wuz learnt in all these exhibits, and wuz destined in the future to bear fruit and bless the world.
12386{_}1659{_}In the Fishery department we see all the products of the great water world that makes up more than half of our earth.
12386{_}1660{_}Every kind of fish that ever swum, from a whale to a minnie, salt water and fresh water fish, and them that are half fish and half animal, and aquatic birds and aquatic plants of all kinds, and plants that seem half way between vegetable and animal.
12386{_}1661{_}Sea grass, shells of all kinds, pearls, pearl-shells, corals, sponges, skins and furs, illustrations, paintings and casts illustrating water life of all kinds, fishing grounds.
12386{_}1662{_}All kinds of boats, nets, traps, rods, reels, lines, fish curing establishments, aquariums, and so and so on and so on, and I might write them "so ons," indefinitely but what would be the use?
12386{_}1663{_}Jest imagine everything that is discovered and brought to light by them that go down to the sea in ships and there it wuz.
12386{_}1664{_}CHAPTER X.
12386{_}1665{_}West of the forestry buildin' growin' right out of the ground is a immense map of the United States covering five acres of ground, gravel walks mark the State and coast lines, and each State is sot out in its own native flowers.
12386{_}1666{_}There it wuz, you could look right down onto it jest like a map, from the rocky shores of Maine down to Florida.
12386{_}1667{_}Josiah wuz simply infatuated with the sight and I myself thought it wuz a great idee and I sez:  "Josiah, this is a plan worthy of Uncle Sam to immortalize what is dearest to him in living colors."
12386{_}1668{_}"Yes, indeed!"
12386{_}1669{_}sez he, and after a minute's thought he added, "Others can foller suit and set them that are dearest to 'em out-doors.
12386{_}1670{_}If I live till another spring, Samantha," sez he firmly, "I will set you out in the paster.
12386{_}1671{_}The dooryard would be too small to do justice to you.
12386{_}1672{_}Ury and I will plant you in the middle of the ten acre lot."
12386{_}1673{_}I wuz touched by the tenderness underlyin' the idee, but sez I, "Have you counted the cost, Josiah?"
12386{_}1674{_}"I know it will cost, you're hefty and big boneded and I'd want you heroic size, but we needn't have your hull frame made in posies, I could plant you in different seeds and raise you like a crop, and sell you in the fall.
12386{_}1675{_}Beans would look well in different colors."
12386{_}1676{_}He see my look of cold irony as he spoke of sellin' me, and added, "Or I could set you out mostly in pusley if you'd ruther, the garden is full of it."
12386{_}1677{_}"I shall never be sot out in pusley, Josiah Allen, I always hated it.
12386{_}1678{_}The hull thing is as crazy as anything you ever undertook."
12386{_}1679{_}"Crazy or not it will be did; summer squash would look well and be equinomical, I could probable train 'em so you'd seem to be holdin' the squashes in your arms."
12386{_}1680{_}"Give up the hull skeem, Josiah Allen; don't try to combine love and economy so clost."
12386{_}1681{_}But he vowed he wouldn't give it up, and I spoze I may see trouble weanin' him from the idee.
12386{_}1682{_}That night whilst I wuz restin' a little in my room after supper, Josiah havin' stayed down in the parlor a spell talkin' to granpa Huff and Billy, Blandina come into my room.
12386{_}1683{_}She wuz all fagged out, but under the fag you could see that expression of perennial good nature and love to man.
12386{_}1684{_}She said she'd been readin' all day to grandpa Huff and as near as I could make out he'd kep' her right down to them blood-curdlin' chapters where they fried the martyrs in ile and briled 'em on grid-irons.
